<L n="1"/><TITLE>The comicall History of the Mer-

<L n="2"/>chant of Venice.</TITLE>

<TLN n="1" /><QLN n="2" />
<L n="2.1"/><SD t="entrance">Enter Anthonio, Salaryno, and Salanio.</SD>

<L n="3"/><MODE t="verse"><TLN n="2" /><QLN n="3" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> IN sooth I know not why I am so sad,
<L n="4"/><TLN n="3" /><QLN n="4" />It wearies me, you say it wearies you;
<L n="5"/><TLN n="4" /><QLN n="5" />But how I caught it, found it, or came by it,
<L n="6"/><TLN n="5" /><QLN n="6" />What stuffe tis made of, whereof it is borne,
<L n="7"/><TLN n="6" /><QLN n="7" />I am to learne: and such a want-wit sadnes
<L n="8"/><TLN n="7" /><QLN n="8" />makes of mee,
<L n="9"/><TLN n="8" /><QLN n="9" />That I haue much adoe to know my selfe.</S>
<L n="10"/><TLN n="9" /><QLN n="10" /><S><SP norm="Salerio">Salerio</SP> Your minde is tossing on the Ocean,
<L n="11"/><TLN n="10" /><QLN n="11" />There where your Argosies with portlie sayle
<L n="12"/><TLN n="11" /><QLN n="12" />Like Signiors and rich Burgars on the flood,
<L n="13"/><TLN n="12" /><QLN n="13" />Or as it were the Pageants of the sea,
<L n="14"/><TLN n="13" /><QLN n="14" />Doe ouer-peere the petty traffiquers
<L n="15"/><TLN n="14" /><QLN n="15" />That cursie to them do them reuerence
<L n="16"/><TLN n="15" /><QLN n="16" />As they flie by them with theyr wouen wings.</S>
<L n="17"/><TLN n="16" /><QLN n="17" /><S><SP norm="Solanio">Solanio</SP> Beleeue mee sir, had I such venture forth,
<L n="18"/><TLN n="17" /><QLN n="18" />The better part of my affections would
<L n="19"/><TLN n="18" /><QLN n="19" />Be with my hopes abroade. I should be still
<L n="20"/><TLN n="19" /><QLN n="20" />Plucking the grasse to know where sits the wind,
<L n="21"/><TLN n="20" /><QLN n="21" />Piring in Maps for ports, and peers and rodes:
<L n="22"/><TLN n="21" /><QLN n="22" />And euery obiect that might make me feare
<L n="23"/><TLN n="22" /><QLN n="23" />Mis-fortune to my ventures, out of doubt
<L n="24"/><TLN n="23" /><QLN n="24" />Would make me sad.</S>
<L n="25"/><TLN n="24" /><QLN n="25" /><S><SP norm="Salerio">Salerio</SP> My wind cooling my broth,
<L n="26"/><TLN n="25" /><QLN n="26" />would blow me to an ague when I thought
<L n="27"/><TLN n="26" /><QLN n="27" />what harme a winde too great might doe at sea.
<L n="28"/><TLN n="27" /><QLN n="28" />I should not see the sandie howre-glasse runne
<L n="29"/><TLN n="28" /><QLN n="29" />But I should thinke of shallowes and of flatts,
<L n="30"/><TLN n="29" /><QLN n="30" />And see my wealthy Andrew docks in sand

<L n="31"/><TLN n="30" /><QLN n="31" />Vayling her high top lower then her ribs
<L n="32"/><TLN n="31" /><QLN n="32" />To kisse her buriall; should I goe to Church
<L n="33"/><TLN n="32" /><QLN n="33" />And see the holy edifice of stone
<L n="34"/><TLN n="33" /><QLN n="34" />And not bethinke me straight of dangerous rocks,
<L n="35"/><TLN n="34" /><QLN n="35" />which touching but my gentle vessels side
<L n="36"/><TLN n="35" /><QLN n="36" />would scatter all her spices on the streame,
<L n="37"/><TLN n="36" /><QLN n="37" />Enrobe the roring waters with my silkes,
<L n="38"/><TLN n="37" /><QLN n="38" />And in a word, but euen now worth this,
<L n="39"/><TLN n="38" /><QLN n="39" />And now worth nothing. Shall I haue the thought
<L n="40"/><TLN n="39" /><QLN n="40" />To thinke on this, and shall I lack the thought
<L n="41"/><TLN n="40" /><QLN n="41" />That such a thing bechaunc'd would make me sad?
<L n="42"/><TLN n="41" /><QLN n="42" />But tell not me, I know Anthonio
<L n="43"/><TLN n="42" /><QLN n="43" />Is sad to thinke vpon his merchandize.</S>
<L n="44"/><TLN n="43" /><QLN n="44" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> Beleeue me no, I thanke my fortune for it
<L n="45"/><TLN n="44" /><QLN n="45" />My ventures are not in one bottome trusted,
<L n="46"/><TLN n="45" /><QLN n="46" />Nor to one place; nor is my whole estate
<L n="47"/><TLN n="46" /><QLN n="47" />Vpon the fortune of this present yeere:
<L n="48"/><TLN n="47" /><QLN n="48" />Therefore my merchandize makes me not sad.</S>
<L n="49"/><TLN n="48" /><QLN n="49" /><S><SP norm="Solanio">Solanio</SP> Why then you are in loue.</S>
<L n="50"/><TLN n="49" /><QLN n="50" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> Fie, fie.</S>
<L n="51"/><TLN n="50" /><QLN n="51" /><S><SP norm="Solanio">Solanio</SP> Not in loue neither: then let vs say you are sad
<L n="52"/><TLN n="51" /><QLN n="52" />Because you are not merry; and twere as easie
<L n="53"/><TLN n="52" /><QLN n="53" />For you to laugh and leape, and say you are merry
<L n="54"/><TLN n="53" /><QLN n="54" />Because you are not sad. Now by two-headed Ianus,
<L n="55"/><TLN n="54" /><QLN n="55" />Nature hath framd strange fellowes in her time:
<L n="56"/><TLN n="55" /><QLN n="56" />Some that will euermore peepe through their eyes,
<L n="57"/><TLN n="56" /><QLN n="57" />And laugh like Parrats at a bagpyper.
<L n="58"/><TLN n="57" /><QLN n="58" />And other of such vinigar aspect,
<L n="59"/><TLN n="58" /><QLN n="59" />That theyle not shew theyr teeth in way of smile
<L n="60"/><TLN n="59" /><QLN n="60" />Though Nestor sweare the iest be laughable.</S>
<TLN n="60" /><QLN n="61" />
<L n="60.1"/><SD t="entrance">Enter Bassanio, Lorenso, and Gratiano.</SD>
<L n="61"/><TLN n="61" /><QLN n="62" /><S><SP norm="Solanio">Solanio</SP> Here comes Bassanio your most noble kinsman,</MODE>
<L n="62"/><TLN n="62" /><QLN n="63" />Gratiano, and Lorenso. Faryewell,
<L n="63"/><TLN n="63" /><QLN n="64" />We leaue you now with better company.</S>
<L n="64"/><TLN n="64" /><QLN n="65" /><S><SP norm="Salerio">Salerio</SP> I would haue staid till I had made you merry,
<L n="65"/><TLN n="65" /><QLN n="66" />If worthier friends had not preuented me.</S>
<L n="66"/><TLN n="66" /><QLN n="67" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> Your worth is very deere in my regard.

<L n="67"/><TLN n="67" /><QLN n="68" />I take it your owne busines calls on you,
<L n="68"/><TLN n="68" /><QLN n="69" />And you embrace th'occasion to depart.</S>
<L n="69"/><TLN n="69" /><QLN n="70" /><S><SP norm="Salerio">Salerio</SP> Good morrow my good Lords.</S>
<L n="70"/><TLN n="70" /><QLN n="71" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> Good signiors both when shal we laugh? say, when?
<L n="71"/><TLN n="71" /><QLN n="72" />You grow exceeding strange: must it be so?</S>
<L n="72"/><TLN n="72" /><QLN n="73" /><S><SP norm="Salerio">Salerio</SP> Weele make our leysures to attend on yours.</S>
<TLN n="73" /><QLN n="74" />
<L n="72.1"/><SD t="exit">Exeunt Salarino, and Solanio.</SD>

<L n="73"/><TLN n="74" /><QLN n="75" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> My Lord Bassanio, since you haue found Anthonio
<L n="74"/><TLN n="75" /><QLN n="76" />We two will leaue you, but at dinner time
<L n="75"/><TLN n="76" /><QLN n="77" />I pray you haue in minde where we must meete.</S>
<L n="76"/><TLN n="77" /><QLN n="78" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> I will not faile you.</S>
<L n="77"/><TLN n="78" /><QLN n="79" /><S><SP norm="Gratiano">Gratiano</SP> You looke not well signior Anthonio,
<L n="78"/><TLN n="79" /><QLN n="80" />You haue too much respect vpon the world:
<L n="79"/><TLN n="80" /><QLN n="81" />They loose it that doe buy it with much care,
<L n="80"/><TLN n="81" /><QLN n="82" />Beleeue me you are meruailously changd.</S>
<L n="81"/><TLN n="82" /><QLN n="83" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> I hold the world but as the world Gratiano,
<L n="82"/><TLN n="83" /><QLN n="84" />A stage, where euery man must play a part,
<L n="83"/><TLN n="84" /><QLN n="85" />And mine a sad one.</S>
<L n="84"/><TLN n="85" /><QLN n="86" /><S><SP norm="Gratiano">Gratiano</SP> Let me play the foole,
<L n="85"/><TLN n="86" /><QLN n="87" />With mirth and laughter let old wrinckles come,
<L n="86"/><TLN n="87" /><QLN n="88" />And let my liuer rather heate with wine
<L n="87"/><TLN n="88" /><QLN n="89" />Then my hart coole with mortifying grones.
<L n="88"/><TLN n="89" /><QLN n="90" />Why should a man whose blood is warme within,
<L n="89"/><TLN n="90" /><QLN n="91" />Sit like his grandsire, cut in Alablaster?
<L n="90"/><TLN n="91" /><QLN n="92" />Sleepe when he wakes? and creepe into the Iaundies
<L n="91"/><TLN n="92" /><QLN n="93" />By beeing peeuish? I tell thee what Anthonio,
<L n="92"/><TLN n="93" /><QLN n="94" />I loue thee, and tis my loue that speakes:
<L n="93"/><TLN n="94" /><QLN n="95" />There are a sort of men whose visages
<L n="94"/><TLN n="95" /><QLN n="96" />Doe creame and mantle like a standing pond,
<L n="95"/><TLN n="96" /><QLN n="97" />And doe a wilful stilnes entertaine,
<L n="96"/><TLN n="97" /><QLN n="98" />With purpose to be drest in an opinion
<L n="97"/><TLN n="98" /><QLN n="99" />Of wisedome, grauitie, profound conceit,
<L n="98"/><TLN n="99" /><QLN n="100" />As who should say, I am sir Oracle,
<L n="99"/><TLN n="100" /><QLN n="101" />And when I ope my lips, let no dogge barke.
<L n="100"/><TLN n="101" /><QLN n="102" />O my Anthonio I doe know of these
<L n="101"/><TLN n="102" /><QLN n="103" />That therefore onely are reputed wise

<L n="102"/><TLN n="103" /><QLN n="104" />For saying nothing; when I am very sure
<L n="103"/><TLN n="104" /><QLN n="105" />If they should speake, would almost dam those eares
<L n="104"/><TLN n="105" /><QLN n="106" />which hearing them would call their brothers fooles,
<L n="105"/><TLN n="106" /><QLN n="107" />Ile tell thee more of this another time.
<L n="106"/><TLN n="107" /><QLN n="108" />But fish not with this melancholy baite
<L n="107"/><TLN n="108" /><QLN n="109" />For this foole gudgin, this opinion:
<L n="108"/><TLN n="109" /><QLN n="110" />Come good Lorenso, faryewell a while,
<L n="109"/><TLN n="110" /><QLN n="111" />Ile end my exhortation after dinner.</S>
<L n="110"/><TLN n="111" /><QLN n="112" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Well, we will leaue you then till dinner time.
<L n="111"/><TLN n="112" /><QLN n="113" />I must be one of these same dumbe wise men,
<L n="112"/><TLN n="113" /><QLN n="114" />For Gratiano neuer lets me speake.</S>
<L n="113"/><TLN n="114" /><QLN n="115" /><S><SP norm="Gratiano">Gratiano</SP> Well keepe me company but two yeeres moe
<L n="114"/><TLN n="115" /><QLN n="116" />Thou shalt not know the sound of thine owne tongue.</S>
<L n="115"/><TLN n="116" /><QLN n="117" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> Far you well, Ile grow a talker for this geare.</S>
<L n="116"/><TLN n="117" /><QLN n="118" /><S><SP norm="Gratiano">Gratiano</SP> Thanks yfaith, for silence is onely commendable
<L n="117"/><TLN n="118" /><QLN n="119" />In a neates togue dried, and a mayde not vendable.</S> 
<SD t="exit"> Exeunt.</SD>
<L n="118"/><TLN n="119" /><QLN n="120" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> It is that any thing now.</S>
<L n="119"/><TLN n="120" /><QLN n="121" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> Gratiano speakes an infinite deale of nothing more then any
<L n="120"/><TLN n="121" /><QLN n="122" />man in all Venice, his reasons are as two graines of wheate hid in
<L n="121"/><TLN n="122" /><QLN n="123" />two bushels of chaffe: you shall seeke all day ere you finde them,
<L n="122"/><TLN n="123" /><QLN n="124" />and when you haue them, they are not worth the search.</S>
<L n="123"/><TLN n="124" /><QLN n="125" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> Well, tell me now what Lady is the same
<L n="124"/><TLN n="125" /><QLN n="126" />To whom you swore a secrete pilgrimage
<L n="125"/><TLN n="126" /><QLN n="127" />That you to day promisd to tell me of.</S>
<L n="126"/><TLN n="127" /><QLN n="128" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> Tis not vnknowne to you Anthonio
<L n="127"/><TLN n="128" /><QLN n="129" />How much I haue disabled mine estate,
<L n="128"/><TLN n="129" /><QLN n="130" />By something showing a more swelling port
<L n="129"/><TLN n="130" /><QLN n="131" />Then my faint meanes would graunt continuance:
<L n="130"/><TLN n="131" /><QLN n="132" />Nor doe I now make mone to be abridg'd
<L n="131"/><TLN n="132" /><QLN n="133" />From such a noble rate, but my cheefe care
<L n="132"/><TLN n="133" /><QLN n="134" />Is to come fairely of from the great debts
<L n="133"/><TLN n="134" /><QLN n="135" />wherein my time something too prodigall
<L n="134"/><TLN n="135" /><QLN n="136" />Hath left me gagd: to you Anthonio
<L n="135"/><TLN n="136" /><QLN n="137" />I owe the most in money and in loue,
<L n="136"/><TLN n="137" /><QLN n="138" />And from your loue I haue a warrantie
<L n="137"/><TLN n="138" /><QLN n="139" />To vnburthen all my plots and purposes
<L n="138"/><TLN n="139" /><QLN n="140" />How to get cleere of all the debts I owe.</S>

<L n="139"/><TLN n="140" /><QLN n="141" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> I pray you good Bassanio let me know it,
<L n="140"/><TLN n="141" /><QLN n="142" />And if it stand as you your selfe still doe,
<L n="141"/><TLN n="142" /><QLN n="143" />within the eye of honour, be assurd
<L n="142"/><TLN n="143" /><QLN n="144" />My purse, my person, my extreamest meanes
<L n="143"/><TLN n="144" /><QLN n="145" />Lie all vnlockt to your occasions.</S>
<L n="144"/><TLN n="145" /><QLN n="146" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> In my schoole dayes, when I had lost one shaft,
<L n="145"/><TLN n="146" /><QLN n="147" />I shot his fellow of the selfe same flight
<L n="146"/><TLN n="147" /><QLN n="148" />The selfe same way, with more aduised watch
<L n="147"/><TLN n="148" /><QLN n="149" />To finde the other forth, and by aduenturing both,
<L n="148"/><TLN n="149" /><QLN n="150" />I oft found both: I vrge this child-hood proofe
<L n="149"/><TLN n="150" /><QLN n="151" />Because what followes is pure innocence.
<L n="150"/><TLN n="151" /><QLN n="152" />I owe you much, and like a wilfull youth
<L n="151"/><TLN n="152" /><QLN n="153" />That which I owe is lost, but if you please
<L n="152"/><TLN n="153" /><QLN n="154" />To shoote another arrow that selfe way
<L n="153"/><TLN n="154" /><QLN n="155" />which you did shoote the first, I doe not doubt,
<L n="154"/><TLN n="155" /><QLN n="156" />As I will watch the ayme or to find both,
<L n="155"/><TLN n="156" /><QLN n="157" />Or bring your latter hazzard bake againe,
<L n="156"/><TLN n="157" /><QLN n="158" />And thankfully rest debter for the first.</S>
<L n="157"/><TLN n="158" /><QLN n="159" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> You know me well, and heerein spend but time
<L n="158"/><TLN n="159" /><QLN n="160" />To wind about my loue with circumstance,
<L n="159"/><TLN n="160" /><QLN n="161" />And out of doubt you doe me now more wrong
<L n="160"/><TLN n="161" /><QLN n="162" />In making question of my vttermost
<L n="161"/><TLN n="162" /><QLN n="163" />Then if you had made wast of all I haue:
<L n="162"/><TLN n="163" /><QLN n="164" />Then doe but say to me what I should doe
<L n="163"/><TLN n="164" /><QLN n="165" />That in your knowledge may by me be done,
<L n="164"/><TLN n="165" /><QLN n="166" />And I am prest vnto it: therefore speake.</S>
<L n="165"/><TLN n="166" /><QLN n="167" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> In Belmont is a Lady richly left,
<L n="166"/><TLN n="167" /><QLN n="168" />And she is faire, and fairer then that word,
<L n="167"/><TLN n="168" /><QLN n="169" />Of wondrous vertues, sometimes from her eyes
<L n="168"/><TLN n="169" /><QLN n="170" />I did receaue faire speechlesse messages:
<L n="169"/><TLN n="170" /><QLN n="171" />Her name is Portia, nothing vndervallewd
<L n="170"/><TLN n="171" /><QLN n="172" />To Catos daughter, Brutus Portia,
<L n="171"/><TLN n="172" /><QLN n="173" />Nor is the wide world ignorant of her worth,
<L n="172"/><TLN n="173" /><QLN n="174" />For the foure winds blow in from euery coast
<L n="173"/><TLN n="174" /><QLN n="175" />Renowned sutors, and her sunny locks
<L n="174"/><TLN n="175" /><QLN n="176" />Hang on her temples like a golden fleece,
<L n="175"/><TLN n="176" /><QLN n="177" />which makes her seat of Belmont Cholchos strond,

<L n="176"/><TLN n="177" /><QLN n="178" />And many Iasons come in quest of her.
<L n="177"/><TLN n="178" /><QLN n="179" />O my Anthonio, had I but the meanes
<L n="178"/><TLN n="179" /><QLN n="180" />To hold a riuall place with one of them,
<L n="179"/><TLN n="180" /><QLN n="181" />I haue a minde presages me such thrift
<L n="180"/><TLN n="181" /><QLN n="182" />That I should questionlesse be fortunate.</S>
<L n="181"/><TLN n="182" /><QLN n="183" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> Thou knowst that all my fortunes are at sea,
<L n="182"/><TLN n="183" /><QLN n="184" />Neither haue I money, nor commoditie
<L n="183"/><TLN n="184" /><QLN n="185" />To raise a present summe, therefore goe forth
<L n="184"/><TLN n="185" /><QLN n="186" />Try what my credite can in Venice doe,
<L n="185"/><TLN n="186" /><QLN n="187" />That shall be rackt euen to the vttermost
<L n="186"/><TLN n="187" /><QLN n="188" />To furnish thee to Belmont to faire Portia.
<L n="187"/><TLN n="188" /><QLN n="189" />Goe presently enquire and so will I
<L n="188"/><TLN n="189" /><QLN n="190" />where money is, and I no question make
<L n="189"/><TLN n="190" /><QLN n="191" />To haue it of my trust, or for my sake.</S>
<SD t="exit"> Exeunt.	</SD>
</SCENE>
<SCENE n="2">
<L n="189.1"/><LD>[Add heading]</LD>
<TLN n="192" /><QLN n="192" />
<L n="189.2"/><SD t="entrance">Enter Portia with her wayting woman Nerrissa.</SD>
<L n="190"/><TLN n="194" /><QLN n="193" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> By my troth Nerrissa, my little body is awearie of this
<L n="191"/><TLN n="195" /><QLN n="194" />great world.</S>
<L n="192"/><TLN n="196" /><QLN n="195" /><S><SP norm="Nerissa">Nerissa</SP> You would be sweet Madam, if your miseries were in the
<L n="193"/><TLN n="197" /><QLN n="196" />same aboundance as your good fortunes are: and yet for ought I
<L n="194"/><TLN n="198" /><QLN n="197" />see, they are as sicke that surfeite with too much, as they that starue
<L n="195"/><TLN n="199" /><QLN n="198" />with nothing; it is no meane happines therfore to be seated in the
<L n="196"/><TLN n="200" /><QLN n="199" />meane, superfluitie comes sooner by white haires, but competen-
<L n="197"/><TLN n="201" /><QLN n="200" />cie liues longer.</S>
<L n="198"/><TLN n="202" /><QLN n="201" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> Good sentences, and well pronounc'd.</S>
<L n="199"/><TLN n="203" /><QLN n="202" /><S><SP norm="Nerissa">Nerissa</SP> They would be better if well followed.</S>
<L n="200"/><TLN n="204" /><QLN n="203" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> If to do were as easie as to know what were good to do,
<L n="201"/><TLN n="205" /><QLN n="204" />Chappels had beene Churches, and poore mens cottages Princes
<L n="202"/><TLN n="206" /><QLN n="205" />Pallaces, it is a good diuine that followes his owne instructions, I
<L n="203"/><TLN n="207" /><QLN n="206" />can easier teach twentie what were good to be done, then to be one
<L n="204"/><TLN n="208" /><QLN n="207" />of the twentie to follow mine owne teaching: the braine may de-
<L n="205"/><TLN n="209" /><QLN n="208" />uise lawes for the blood, but a hote temper leapes ore a colde de-
<L n="206"/><TLN n="210" /><QLN n="209" />cree, such a hare is madnes the youth, to skippe ore the meshes of
<L n="207"/><TLN n="211" /><QLN n="210" />good counsaile the cripple; but this reasoning is not in the fashion
<L n="208"/><TLN n="212" /><QLN n="211" />to choose mee a husband, ^o mee the word choose, I may neyther
<L n="209"/><TLN n="213" /><QLN n="212" />choose who I would, nor refuse who I dislike, so is the will of a ly-
<L n="210"/><TLN n="214" /><QLN n="213" />uing daughter curbd by the will of a deade father: is it not harde

<L n="211"/><TLN n="215" /><QLN n="214" />Nerrissa, that I cannot choose one, nor refuse none.</S>

<L n="303"/><TLN n="312" /><QLN n="308" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> For three months, well.</S>

<L n="311"/><TLN n="320" /><QLN n="316" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> Your aunswere to that.</S>
<L n="312"/><TLN n="321" /><QLN n="317" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> Anthonio is a good man.</S>
<L n="313"/><TLN n="322" /><QLN n="318" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> Haue you heard any imputation to the contrary.</S>
<L n="314"/><TLN n="323" /><QLN n="319" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> Ho no, no, no, no: my meaning in saying hee is
<L n="315"/><TLN n="324" /><QLN n="320" />a good man, is to haue you vnderstand mee that hee is sufficient,
<L n="316"/><TLN n="325" /><QLN n="321" />yet his meanes are in supposition: hee hath an Argosie bound

<L n="318"/><TLN n="327" /><QLN n="323" />on the Ryalta, hee hath a third at Mexico, a fourth for England,

<L n="319"/><TLN n="328" /><QLN n="324" />and other ventures he hath squandred abroade, but ships are but
<L n="320"/><TLN n="329" /><QLN n="325" />boordes, Saylers but men, there be land rats, and water rats, water
<L n="321"/><TLN n="330" /><QLN n="326" />theeues, and land theeues, I meane Pyrats, and then there is the
<L n="322"/><TLN n="331" /><QLN n="327" />perrill of waters, windes, and rockes: the man is notwithstanding
<L n="323"/><TLN n="332" /><QLN n="328" />sufficient, three thousand ducats, I thinke I may take his bond.</S>
<L n="324"/><TLN n="333" /><QLN n="329" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> Be assurd you may.</S>
<L n="325"/><TLN n="334" /><QLN n="330" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> I will be assurd I may: and that I may bee assured, I will
<L n="326"/><TLN n="335" /><QLN n="331" />bethinke mee, may I speake with Anthonio?</S>
<L n="327"/><TLN n="336" /><QLN n="332" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> Yf it please you to dine with vs.</S>
<L n="328"/><TLN n="337" /><QLN n="333" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> Yes, to smell porke, to eate of the habitation which your

<L n="331"/><TLN n="340" /><QLN n="336" />but I will not eate with you, drinke with you, nor pray with you.
<L n="332"/><TLN n="341" /><QLN n="337" />What newes on the Ryalto, who is he comes heere?</S>
<TLN n="342" /><QLN n="338" />
<L n="332.1"/><SD t="entrance">Enter Anthonio.</SD>
<L n="333"/><TLN n="343" /><QLN n="339" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> This is signior Anthonio.</S>
<L n="334"/><TLN n="344" /><QLN n="340" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> How like a fawning publican he lookes.
<L n="335"/><TLN n="345" /><QLN n="341" />I hate him for he is a Christian:
<L n="336"/><TLN n="346" /><QLN n="342" />But more, for that in low simplicitie

<L n="360"/><TLN n="370" /><QLN n="366" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP>JI, I, three thousand ducats.</S>

<L n="362"/><TLN n="372" /><QLN n="368" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> I had forgot, three months, you told me so.

<L n="365"/><TLN n="375" /><QLN n="371" />Vpon aduantage.</S>
<L n="366"/><TLN n="376" /><QLN n="372" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> I doe neuer vse it.</S>
<L n="367"/><TLN n="377" /><QLN n="373" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> When Iacob grazd his Vncle Labans Sheepe,
<L n="368"/><TLN n="378" /><QLN n="374" />This Iacob from our holy Abram was
<L n="369"/><TLN n="379" /><QLN n="375" />(As his wise mother wrought in his behalfe)

<L n="371"/><TLN n="381" /><QLN n="377" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> And what of him, did he take interrest?</S>

<L n="387"/><TLN n="397" /><QLN n="393" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> This was a venture sir that Iacob serud for,

<L n="396"/><TLN n="406" /><QLN n="402" />An euill soule producing holy witnes

<L n="399"/><TLN n="409" /><QLN n="405" />O what a goodly out-side falshood hath.</S>
<L n="400"/><TLN n="410" /><QLN n="406" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> Three thousand ducats, tis a good round summe.
<L n="401"/><TLN n="411" /><QLN n="407" />Three months from twelue, then let me see the rate.</S>
<L n="402"/><TLN n="412" /><QLN n="408" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> Well Shylocke, shall we be beholding to you?</S>
<L n="403"/><TLN n="413" /><QLN n="409" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> Signior Anthonio, manie a time and oft

<L n="426"/><TLN n="436" /><QLN n="432" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP>J am as like to call thee so againe,

<L n="480.3"/><SD t="entrance">Enter Morochus a tawnie Moore all in white, and three

<L n="481"/><TLN n="495" /><QLN n="491" /><S><SP norm="Morocco">Morocco</SP> Mislike me not for my complexion,
<L n="482"/><TLN n="496" /><QLN n="492" />The shadowed liuerie of the burnisht sunne,
<L n="483"/><TLN n="497" /><QLN n="493" />To whom I am a neighbour, and neere bred.
<L n="484"/><TLN n="498" /><QLN n="494" />Bring me the fayrest creature North-ward borne,
<L n="485"/><TLN n="499" /><QLN n="495" />Where Phaebus fire scarce thawes the ysicles,
<L n="486"/><TLN n="500" /><QLN n="496" />And let vs make incyzion for your loue,
<L n="487"/><TLN n="501" /><QLN n="497" />To proue whose blood is reddest, his or mine.
<L n="488"/><TLN n="502" /><QLN n="498" />I tell thee Lady this aspect of mine
<L n="489"/><TLN n="503" /><QLN n="499" />Hath feard the valiant, (by my loue I sweare)
<L n="490"/><TLN n="504" /><QLN n="500" />The best regarded Virgins of our Clyme
<L n="491"/><TLN n="505" /><QLN n="501" />Haue lou'd it to: I would not change this hue,
<L n="492"/><TLN n="506" /><QLN n="502" />Except to steale your thoughts my gentle Queene.</S>
<L n="493"/><TLN n="507" /><QLN n="503" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> In termes of choyse I am not soly led
<L n="494"/><TLN n="508" /><QLN n="504" />By nice direction of a maydens eyes:
<L n="495"/><TLN n="509" /><QLN n="505" />Besides, the lottrie of my destenie
<L n="496"/><TLN n="510" /><QLN n="506" />Barrs me the right of voluntary choosing:
<L n="497"/><TLN n="511" /><QLN n="507" />But if my Father had not scanted me,

<L n="498"/><TLN n="512" /><QLN n="508" />And hedgd me by his wit to yeeld my selfe
<L n="499"/><TLN n="513" /><QLN n="509" />His wife, who winnes me by that meanes I told you,
<L n="500"/><TLN n="514" /><QLN n="510" />Your selfe (renowned Prince) than stoode as faire
<L n="501"/><TLN n="515" /><QLN n="511" />As any commer I haue look'd on yet

<L n="530"/><TLN n="546" /><QLN n="542" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> Certainely, my conscience will serue me to runne from
<L n="531"/><TLN n="547" /><QLN n="543" />this Iewe my Maister: the fiend is at mine elbow, and tempts me,
<L n="532"/><TLN n="548" /><QLN n="544" />saying to me, Iobbe, Launcelet Jobbe, good Launcelet, or good Iobbe,

<L n="539"/><TLN n="555" /><QLN n="551" />well, my conscience hanging about the necke of my heart, sayes
<L n="540"/><TLN n="556" /><QLN n="552" />very wisely to mee: my honest friend Launcelet beeing an honest
<L n="541"/><TLN n="557" /><QLN n="553" />mans sonne, or rather an honest womans sonne, for indeede my

<L n="973"/><TLN n="1002" /><QLN n="998" />Fareyouwell, your sute is cold.</QUOTE></MODE></S></INDENT>

<L n="1313"/><TLN n="1358" /><QLN n="1352" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> So may the outward showes be least themselues,
<L n="1314"/><TLN n="1359" /><QLN n="1353" />The world is still deceau'd with ornament
<L n="1315"/><TLN n="1360" /><QLN n="1354" />In Law, what plea so tainted and corrupt,
<L n="1316"/><TLN n="1361" /><QLN n="1355" />But being season'd with a gracious voyce,
<L n="1317"/><TLN n="1362" /><QLN n="1356" />Obscures the show of euill. In religion
<L n="1318"/><TLN n="1363" /><QLN n="1357" />What damned error but some sober brow
<L n="1319"/><TLN n="1364" /><QLN n="1358" />will blesse it, and approue it with a text,
<L n="1320"/><TLN n="1365" /><QLN n="1359" />Hiding the grosnes with faire ornament:
<L n="1321"/><TLN n="1366" /><QLN n="1360" />There is no voyce so simple, but assumes
<L n="1322"/><TLN n="1367" /><QLN n="1361" />Some marke of vertue on his outward parts;
<L n="1323"/><TLN n="1368" /><QLN n="1362" />How many cowards whose harts are all as false
<L n="1324"/><TLN n="1369" /><QLN n="1363" />As stayers of sand, weare yet vpon their chins
<L n="1325"/><TLN n="1370" /><QLN n="1364" />The beards of Hercules and frowning Mars,
<L n="1326"/><TLN n="1371" /><QLN n="1365" />who inward searcht, haue lyuers white as milke,
<L n="1327"/><TLN n="1372" /><QLN n="1366" />And these assume but valours excrement
<L n="1328"/><TLN n="1373" /><QLN n="1367" />To render them redoubted. Looke on beauty,
<L n="1329"/><TLN n="1374" /><QLN n="1368" />And you shall see tis purchast by the weight,
<L n="1330"/><TLN n="1375" /><QLN n="1369" />which therein works a miracle in nature,
<L n="1331"/><TLN n="1376" /><QLN n="1370" />Making them lightest that weare most of it:
<L n="1332"/><TLN n="1377" /><QLN n="1371" />So are those crisped snaky golden locks
<L n="1333"/><TLN n="1378" /><QLN n="1372" />which maketh such wanton gambols with the wind
<L n="1334"/><TLN n="1379" /><QLN n="1373" />Vpon supposed fairenes, often knowne
<L n="1335"/><TLN n="1380" /><QLN n="1374" />To be the dowry of a second head,
<L n="1336"/><TLN n="1381" /><QLN n="1375" />The scull that bred them in the Sepulcher.
<L n="1337"/><TLN n="1382" /><QLN n="1376" />Thus ornament is but the guiled shore
<L n="1338"/><TLN n="1383" /><QLN n="1377" />To a most dangerous sea: the beautious scarfe
<L n="1339"/><TLN n="1384" /><QLN n="1378" />vailing an Indian beauty; In a word,
<L n="1340"/><TLN n="1385" /><QLN n="1379" />The seeming truth which cunning times put on
<L n="1341"/><TLN n="1386" /><QLN n="1380" />To intrap the wisest. Therefore then thou gaudy gold,
<L n="1342"/><TLN n="1387" /><QLN n="1381" />Hard food for Midas, I will none of thee,

<L n="1343"/><TLN n="1388" /><QLN n="1382" />Nor none of thee thou pale and common drudge
<L n="1344"/><TLN n="1389" /><QLN n="1383" />tweene man and man: but thou, thou meager lead
<L n="1345"/><TLN n="1390" /><QLN n="1384" />which rather threatenst then dost promise ought,
<L n="1346"/><TLN n="1391" /><QLN n="1385" />thy palenes moues me more then eloquence,
<L n="1347"/><TLN n="1392" /><QLN n="1386" />and heere choose I, ioy be the consequence.</S>
<L n="1348"/><TLN n="1393" /><QLN n="1387" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> How all the other passions fleet to ayre,

<L n="1354"/><TLN n="1399" /><QLN n="1393" />for feare I surfeit.</S>
<L n="1355"/><TLN n="1400" /><QLN n="1394" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> What finde I heere?

<L n="1372"/><TLN n="1417" /><QLN n="1411" /><INDENT l="5">You that choose not by the view
<L n="1373"/><TLN n="1418" /><QLN n="1412" />Chaunce as faire, and choose as true:

<L n="1380"/><TLN n="1425" /><QLN n="1419" />A gentle scroule: Faire Lady, by your leaue,

<L n="1390"/><TLN n="1435" /><QLN n="1429" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> You see me Lord Bassanio where I stand,

<L n="1532"/><TLN n="1579" /><QLN n="1573" />that he did owe him: and I know my lord,

<L n="1534"/><TLN n="1581" /><QLN n="1575" />it will goe hard with poore Anthonio.</S>
<L n="1535"/><TLN n="1582" /><QLN n="1576" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> Is it your deere friend that is thus in trouble?</S>
<L n="1536"/><TLN n="1583" /><QLN n="1577" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> The deerest friend to me, the kindest man,
<L n="1537"/><TLN n="1584" /><QLN n="1578" />the best conditiond and vnwearied spirit
<L n="1538"/><TLN n="1585" /><QLN n="1579" />in dooing curtesies: and one in whom
<L n="1539"/><TLN n="1586" /><QLN n="1580" />the auncient Romaine honour more appeares
<L n="1540"/><TLN n="1587" /><QLN n="1581" />then any that drawes breath in Italie.</S>
<L n="1541"/><TLN n="1588" /><QLN n="1582" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> What summe owes he the Iew?</S>
<L n="1542"/><TLN n="1589" /><QLN n="1583" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> For me three thousand ducats.</S>
<L n="1543"/><TLN n="1590" /><QLN n="1584" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> What no more, pay him six thousand, & deface the bond:
<L n="1544"/><TLN n="1591" /><QLN n="1585" />double sixe thousand, and then treble that,
<L n="1545"/><TLN n="1592" /><QLN n="1586" />before a friend of this discription
<L n="1546"/><TLN n="1593" /><QLN n="1587" />shall lose a haire through Bassanios fault.
<L n="1547"/><TLN n="1594" /><QLN n="1588" />First goe with me to Church, and call me wife,
<L n="1548"/><TLN n="1595" /><QLN n="1589" />and then away to Venice to your friend:
<L n="1549"/><TLN n="1596" /><QLN n="1590" />for neuer shall you lie by Portias side
<L n="1550"/><TLN n="1597" /><QLN n="1591" />with an vnquiet soule. You shall haue gold
<L n="1551"/><TLN n="1598" /><QLN n="1592" />to pay the petty debt twenty times ouer.
<L n="1552"/><TLN n="1599" /><QLN n="1593" />When it is payd, bring your true friend along,
<L n="1553"/><TLN n="1600" /><QLN n="1594" />my mayd Nerrissa, and my selfe meane time
<L n="1554"/><TLN n="1601" /><QLN n="1595" />will liue as maydes and widdowes; come away,
<L n="1555"/><TLN n="1602" /><QLN n="1596" />for you shall hence vpon your wedding day:
<L n="1556"/><TLN n="1603" /><QLN n="1597" />bid your freends welcome, show a merry cheere,
<L n="1557"/><TLN n="1604" /><QLN n="1598" />since you are deere bought, I will loue you deere.
<L n="1558"/><TLN n="1605" /><QLN n="1599" />But let me heare the letter of your friend.

<L n="1559"/><TLN n="1606" /><QLN n="1600" /><MODE t="prose"><QUOTE> Sweet Bassanio, my ships haue all miscaried, my Creditors growe <TLN n="1607" /><QLN n="1601" />cruell, my estate is very low, my bond to the Iewe is forfaite, and since in <TLN n="1608" /><QLN n="1602" />paying it, it is impossible I should liue, all debts are cleerd betweene you</QUOTE></MODE>

<L n="1560"/><TLN n="1609" /><QLN n="1603" /><MODE t="prose"><QUOTE> and I if I might but see you at my death: notwithstanding, vse your plea- <TLN n="1610" /><QLN n="1604" />sure, if your loue do not perswade you to come, let not my letter.</QUOTE></MODE></S>

<L n="1561"/><TLN n="1611" /><QLN n="1605" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> O loue! dispatch all busines and be gone.</S>
<L n="1562"/><TLN n="1612" /><QLN n="1606" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> Since I haue your good leaue to goe away,
<L n="1563"/><TLN n="1613" /><QLN n="1607" />I will make hast; but till I come againe,
<L n="1564"/><TLN n="1614" /><QLN n="1608" />no bed shall ere be guiltie of my stay,
<L n="1565"/><TLN n="1615" /><QLN n="1609" />nor rest be interposer twixt vs twaine.</S>

<TLN n="1616" /><QLN n="1610" />	
<SD t="exit"> Exeunt.	</SD>

<SCENE n="5">

<L n="1691"/><TLN n="1748" /><QLN n="1742" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> Yes truly, for looke you, the sinnes of the Father are to
<L n="1692"/><TLN n="1749" /><QLN n="1743" />be laid vpon the children, therefore I promise you, I feare you, I

<L n="1697"/><TLN n="1754" /><QLN n="1748" /><S><SP norm="Jessica">Jessica</SP> And what hope is that I pray thee?</S>

<L n="1699"/><TLN n="1756" /><QLN n="1750" />not, that you are not the Iewes daughter.</S>
<L n="1700"/><TLN n="1757" /><QLN n="1751" /><S><SP norm="Jessica">Jessica</SP> That were a kind of bastard hope in deede, so the sinnes

<L n="1702"/><TLN n="1759" /><QLN n="1753" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> Truly then I feare you are damnd both by father and

<L n="1704"/><TLN n="1761" /><QLN n="1755" />your mother; well, you are gone both wayes.</S>
<L n="1705"/><TLN n="1762" /><QLN n="1756" /><S><SP norm="Jessica">Jessica</SP> I shall be sau'd by my husband, he hath made me a Chri

<L n="1709"/><TLN n="1766" /><QLN n="1760" />of Christians will raise the price of Hogs, if we grow all to be pork
<L n="1710"/><TLN n="1767" /><QLN n="1761" />eaters, we shall not shortly haue a rasher on the coles for mony.</S>
<TLN n="1768" /><QLN n="1762" />

<L n="1713"/><TLN n="1771" /><QLN n="1765" />get my wife into corners?</S>
<L n="1714"/><TLN n="1772" /><QLN n="1766" /><S><SP norm="Jessica">Jessica</SP> Nay, you neede not feare vs Lorenzo, Launcelet and I are
<L n="1715"/><TLN n="1773" /><QLN n="1767" />out, he tells me flatly there's no mercy for mee in heauen, because
<L n="1716"/><TLN n="1774" /><QLN n="1768" />I am a Iewes daughter: and he sayes you are no good member of
<L n="1717"/><TLN n="1775" /><QLN n="1769" />the common-wealth, for in conuerting Iewes to Christians, you
<L n="1718"/><TLN n="1776" /><QLN n="1770" />raise the price of porke.</S>
<L n="1719"/><TLN n="1777" /><QLN n="1771" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> I shall aunswere that better to the common-wealth than
<L n="1720"/><TLN n="1778" /><QLN n="1772" />you can the getting vp of the Negroes belly: the Moore is with
<L n="1721"/><TLN n="1779" /><QLN n="1773" />child by you Launcelet?</S>
<L n="1722"/><TLN n="1780" /><QLN n="1774" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> It is much that the Moore should be more then rea-
<L n="1723"/><TLN n="1781" /><QLN n="1775" />son: but if she be lesse then an honest woman, she is indeede more
<L n="1724"/><TLN n="1782" /><QLN n="1776" />then I tooke her for.</S>
<L n="1725"/><TLN n="1783" /><QLN n="1777" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> How euery foole can play vpon the word, I thinke the
<L n="1726"/><TLN n="1784" /><QLN n="1778" />best grace of wit will shortly turne into silence, and discourse grow
<L n="1727"/><TLN n="1785" /><QLN n="1779" />commendable in none onely but Parrats: goe in sirra, bid them
<L n="1728"/><TLN n="1786" /><QLN n="1780" />prepare for dinner?</S>
<L n="1729"/><TLN n="1787" /><QLN n="1781" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> That is done sir, they haue all stomacks?</S>
<L n="1730"/><TLN n="1788" /><QLN n="1782" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Goodly Lord what a wit snapper are you, than bid them
<L n="1731"/><TLN n="1789" /><QLN n="1783" />prepare dinner?</S>

<L n="1732"/><TLN n="1790" /><QLN n="1784" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> That is done to sir, onely couer is the word.</S>
<L n="1733"/><TLN n="1791" /><QLN n="1785" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Will you couer than sir?</S>
<L n="1734"/><TLN n="1792" /><QLN n="1786" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> Not so sir neither, I know my duty.</S>
<L n="1735"/><TLN n="1793" /><QLN n="1787" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Yet more quarrelling with occasion, wilt thou shewe
<L n="1736"/><TLN n="1794" /><QLN n="1788" />the whole wealth of thy wit in an instant; I pray thee vnderstand a
<L n="1737"/><TLN n="1795" /><QLN n="1789" />plaine man in his plaine meaning: goe to thy fellowes, bid them
<L n="1738"/><TLN n="1796" /><QLN n="1790" />couer the table, serue in the meate, and we will come in to dinner.</S>
<L n="1739"/><TLN n="1797" /><QLN n="1791" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> For the table sir, it shall be seru'd in, for the meate sir, it
<L n="1740"/><TLN n="1798" /><QLN n="1792" />shall be couerd, for your comming in to dinner sir, why let it be as
<L n="1741"/><TLN n="1799" /><QLN n="1793" />humors and conceites shall gouerne.</S> 
<SD t="exit"> Exit Clowne. </SD>
<L n="1742"/><TLN n="1800" /><QLN n="1794" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> O deare discretion, how his words are suted,
<L n="1743"/><TLN n="1801" /><QLN n="1795" />The foole hath planted in his memorie
<L n="1744"/><TLN n="1802" /><QLN n="1796" />an Armie of good words, and I doe know
<L n="1745"/><TLN n="1803" /><QLN n="1797" />a many fooles that stand in better place,
<L n="1746"/><TLN n="1804" /><QLN n="1798" />garnisht like him, that for a tricksie word
<L n="1747"/><TLN n="1805" /><QLN n="1799" />defie the matter: how cherst thou Iessica,
<L n="1748"/><TLN n="1806" /><QLN n="1800" />And now good sweet say thy opinion,
<L n="1749"/><TLN n="1807" /><QLN n="1801" />How doost thou like the Lord Bassanios wife?</S>
<L n="1750"/><TLN n="1808" /><QLN n="1802" /><S><SP norm="Jessica">Jessica</SP> Past all expressing, it is very meete
<L n="1751"/><TLN n="1809" /><QLN n="1803" />the Lord Bassanio liue an vpright life
<L n="1752"/><TLN n="1810" /><QLN n="1804" />For hauing such a blessing in his Lady,
<L n="1753"/><TLN n="1811" /><QLN n="1805" />he findes the ioyes of heauen heere on earth,
<L n="1754"/><TLN n="1812" /><QLN n="1806" />And if on earth he doe not meane it, it
<L n="1755"/><TLN n="1813" /><QLN n="1807" />in reason he should neuer come to heauen?
<L n="1756"/><TLN n="1814" /><QLN n="1808" />Why, if two Gods should play some heauenly match,
<L n="1757"/><TLN n="1815" /><QLN n="1809" />and on the wager lay two earthly women,
<L n="1758"/><TLN n="1816" /><QLN n="1810" />And Portia one: there must be somthing else
<L n="1759"/><TLN n="1817" /><QLN n="1811" />paund with the other, for the poore rude world
<L n="1760"/><TLN n="1818" /><QLN n="1812" />hath not her fellow.</S>
<L n="1761"/><TLN n="1819" /><QLN n="1813" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Euen such a husband
<L n="1762"/><TLN n="1820" /><QLN n="1814" />hast thou of me, as she is for wife.</S>
<L n="1763"/><TLN n="1821" /><QLN n="1815" /><S><SP norm="Jessica">Jessica</SP> Nay, but aske my opinion to of that?</S>
<L n="1764"/><TLN n="1822" /><QLN n="1816" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> I will anone, first let vs goe to dinner?</S>
<L n="1765"/><TLN n="1823" /><QLN n="1817" /><S><SP norm="Jessica">Jessica</SP> Nay, let me praise you while I haue a stomack?</S>
<L n="1766"/><TLN n="1824" /><QLN n="1818" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> No pray thee, let it serue for table talke,
<L n="1767"/><TLN n="1825" /><QLN n="1819" />Then how so mere thou speakst mong other things,
<L n="1768"/><TLN n="1826" /><QLN n="1820" />I shall disgest it?</S>

<L n="1769"/><TLN n="1827" /><QLN n="1821" /><S><SP norm="Jessica">Jessica</SP> Well, ile set you forth.</S>
<SD t="exit"> Exit.	</SD>

<L n="1770"/><TLN n="1830" /><QLN n="1824" /><S><SP norm="Duke">Duke</SP> What, is Anthonio heere?</S>
<L n="1771"/><TLN n="1831" /><QLN n="1825" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> Ready, so please your grace?</S>
<L n="1772"/><TLN n="1832" /><QLN n="1826" /><S><SP norm="Duke">Duke</SP> I am sorry for thee, thou art come to aunswere
<L n="1773"/><TLN n="1833" /><QLN n="1827" />a stonie aduersarie, an inhumaine wretch,
<L n="1774"/><TLN n="1834" /><QLN n="1828" />vncapable of pitty, voyd, and empty
<L n="1775"/><TLN n="1835" /><QLN n="1829" />from any dram of mercie.</S>
<L n="1776"/><TLN n="1836" /><QLN n="1830" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> I haue heard

<L n="1778"/><TLN n="1838" /><QLN n="1832" />his rigorous course; but since he stands obdurate,
<L n="1779"/><TLN n="1839" /><QLN n="1833" />And that no lawfull meanes can carry me
<L n="1780"/><TLN n="1840" /><QLN n="1834" />out of his enuies reach, I doe oppose
<L n="1781"/><TLN n="1841" /><QLN n="1835" />my patience to his furie, and am armd

<L n="1784"/><TLN n="1844" /><QLN n="1838" /><S><SP norm="Duke">Duke</SP> Goe one and call the Iew into the Court.</S>

<TLN n="1846" /><QLN n="1840" />
<L n="1785.1"/><SD t="entrance">Enter Shylocke.</SD>
<L n="1786"/><TLN n="1847" /><QLN n="1841" /><S><SP norm="Duke">Duke</SP> Make roome, and let him stand before our face.
<L n="1787"/><TLN n="1848" /><QLN n="1842" />Shylocke the world thinks, and I thinke so to
<L n="1788"/><TLN n="1849" /><QLN n="1843" />that thou but leadest this fashion of thy mallice
<L n="1789"/><TLN n="1850" /><QLN n="1844" />to the last houre of act, and then tis thought
<L n="1790"/><TLN n="1851" /><QLN n="1845" />thowlt shew thy mercy and remorse more strange,

<L n="1792"/><TLN n="1853" /><QLN n="1847" />and where thou now exacts the penalty,

<L n="1794"/><TLN n="1855" /><QLN n="1849" />thou wilt not onely loose the forfaiture,
<L n="1795"/><TLN n="1856" /><QLN n="1850" />but toucht with humaine gentlenes and loue:
<L n="1796"/><TLN n="1857" /><QLN n="1851" />Forgiue a moytie of the principall,
<L n="1797"/><TLN n="1858" /><QLN n="1852" />glauncing an eye of pitty on his losses
<L n="1798"/><TLN n="1859" /><QLN n="1853" />that haue of late so hudled on his backe,
<L n="1799"/><TLN n="1860" /><QLN n="1854" />Enow to presse a royall Merchant downe;
<L n="1800"/><TLN n="1861" /><QLN n="1855" />And pluck comiseration of this states
<L n="1801"/><TLN n="1862" /><QLN n="1856" />from brassie bosomes and rough harts of flints,
<L n="1802"/><TLN n="1863" /><QLN n="1857" />from stubborne Turkes, and Tarters neuer traind

<L n="1803"/><TLN n="1864" /><QLN n="1858" />to offices of tender curtesie:
<L n="1804"/><TLN n="1865" /><QLN n="1859" />We all expect a gentle aunswere Iewe?</S>
<L n="1805"/><TLN n="1866" /><QLN n="1860" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> I haue possest your grace of what I purpose,
<L n="1806"/><TLN n="1867" /><QLN n="1861" />and by our holy Sabaoth haue I sworne
<L n="1807"/><TLN n="1868" /><QLN n="1862" />to haue the due and forfet of my bond,
<L n="1808"/><TLN n="1869" /><QLN n="1863" />if you deny it, let the danger light
<L n="1809"/><TLN n="1870" /><QLN n="1864" />vpon your charter and your Citties freedome?
<L n="1810"/><TLN n="1871" /><QLN n="1865" />Youle aske me why I rather choose to haue
<L n="1811"/><TLN n="1872" /><QLN n="1866" />a weight of carrion flesh, then to receaue
<L n="1812"/><TLN n="1873" /><QLN n="1867" />three thousand ducats: Ile not aunswer that?
<L n="1813"/><TLN n="1874" /><QLN n="1868" />But say it is my humour, is it aunswerd?
<L n="1814"/><TLN n="1875" /><QLN n="1869" />What if my house be troubled with a Rat,
<L n="1815"/><TLN n="1876" /><QLN n="1870" />and I be pleasd to giue ten thousand ducats
<L n="1816"/><TLN n="1877" /><QLN n="1871" />to haue it baind? what, are you aunswerd yet?
<L n="1817"/><TLN n="1878" /><QLN n="1872" />Some men there are loue not a gaping pigge?
<L n="1818"/><TLN n="1879" /><QLN n="1873" />Some that are mad if they behold a Cat?
<L n="1819"/><TLN n="1880" /><QLN n="1874" />And others when the bagpipe sings ith nose,
<L n="1820"/><TLN n="1881" /><QLN n="1875" />cannot containe their vrine for affection.
<L n="1821"/><TLN n="1882" /><QLN n="1876" />Maisters of passion swayes it to the moode
<L n="1822"/><TLN n="1883" /><QLN n="1877" />of what it likes or loathes, now for your aunswer:
<L n="1823"/><TLN n="1884" /><QLN n="1878" />As there is no firme reason to be rendred
<L n="1824"/><TLN n="1885" /><QLN n="1879" />why he cannot abide a gaping pigge?

<L n="1826"/><TLN n="1887" /><QLN n="1881" />why he a woollen bagpipe: but of force

<L n="1833"/><TLN n="1894" /><QLN n="1888" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> This is no aunswer thou vnfeeling man,

<L n="1839"/><TLN n="1900" /><QLN n="1894" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> What wouldst thou haue a serpent sting thee twice?</S>

<L n="1840"/><TLN n="1901" /><QLN n="1895" /><S><SP norm="Antonio">Antonio</SP> I pray you think you question with the Iewe,

<L n="1889.1"/><SD t="entrance">Enter Nerrissa.</SD>

<L n="1892"/><TLN n="1954" /><QLN n="1948" /><S><SP norm="Bassanio">Bassanio</SP> Why doost thou whet thy knife so earnestly?</S>

<L n="1898"/><TLN n="1960" /><QLN n="1954" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> No, none that thou hast wit enough to make.</S>
<L n="1899"/><TLN n="1961" /><QLN n="1955" /><S><SP norm="Gratiano">Gratiano</SP> O be thou damnd, inexecrable dogge,
<L n="1900"/><TLN n="1962" /><QLN n="1956" />And for thy life let iustice be accusd;
<L n="1901"/><TLN n="1963" /><QLN n="1957" />Thou almost mak'st me wauer in my faith,

<L n="1904"/><TLN n="1966" /><QLN n="1960" />into the trunks of men: Thy currish spirit

<L n="1909"/><TLN n="1971" /><QLN n="1965" />are woluish, bloody, staru'd, and rauenous.</S>
<L n="1910"/><TLN n="1972" /><QLN n="1966" /><S><SP norm="Shylock">Shylock</SP> Till thou canst raile the seale from off my bond,

<L n="1912"/><TLN n="1974" /><QLN n="1968" />Repaire thy wit good youth, or it will fall

<L n="1913"/><TLN n="1975" /><QLN n="1969" />to curelesse ruine. I stand heere for law.</S>
<L n="1914"/><TLN n="1976" /><QLN n="1970" /><S><SP norm="Duke">Duke</SP> This letter from Bellario doth commend
<L n="1915"/><TLN n="1977" /><QLN n="1971" />a young and learned Doctor to our Court:
<L n="1916"/><TLN n="1978" /><QLN n="1972" />Where is he?</S>
<L n="1917"/><TLN n="1979" /><QLN n="1973" /><S><SP norm="Nerissa">Nerissa</SP> He attendeth here hard by
<L n="1918"/><TLN n="1980" /><QLN n="1974" />to know your aunswer whether youle admit him.</S>
<L n="1919"/><TLN n="1981" /><QLN n="1975" /><S><SP norm="Duke">Duke</SP> With all my hart: some three or foure of you
<L n="1920"/><TLN n="1982" /><QLN n="1976" />goe giue him curteous conduct to this place,
<L n="1921"/><TLN n="1983" /><QLN n="1977" />meane time the Court shall heare Bellarios letter.

<L n="1922"/><TLN n="1984" /><QLN n="1978" /><MODE t="prose"><QUOTE>Your Grace shall vnderstand, that at the receit of your letter I <TLN n="1985" /><QLN n="1979" />am very sicke, but in the instant that your messenger came, in lo- <TLN n="1986" /><QLN n="1980" />uing visitation was with me a young Doctor of Rome, his name is <TLN n="1987" /><QLN n="1981" />Balthazer: I acquainted him with the cause in c_otrouersie between <TLN n="1988" /><QLN n="1982" />the Iew and Anthonio the Merchant, wee turnd ore many bookes <TLN n="1989" /><QLN n="1983" />together, hee is furnished with my opinion, which bettered with <TLN n="1990" /><QLN n="1984" />his owne learning, the greatnes whereof I cannot enough com- <TLN n="1991" /><QLN n="1985" />mend, comes with him at my importunitie, to fill vp your graces <TLN n="1992" /><QLN n="1986" />request in my stead. I beseech you let his lacke of yeeres be no im- <TLN n="1993" /><QLN n="1987" />pediment to let him lacke a reuerend estimation, for I neuer knew <TLN n="1994" /><QLN n="1988" />so young a body with so olde a head: I leaue him to your gracious <TLN n="1995" /><QLN n="1989" />acceptance, whose tryall shall better publish his commendation.</QUOTE></MODE></S>

<L n="1944"/><TLN n="2018" /><QLN n="2012" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> The qualitie of mercie is not straind,
<L n="1945"/><TLN n="2019" /><QLN n="2013" />it droppeth as the gentle raine from heauen

<L n="1949"/><TLN n="2023" /><QLN n="2017" />the throned Monarch better then his crowne.
<L n="1950"/><TLN n="2024" /><QLN n="2018" />His scepter showes the force of temporall power,

<L n="2264"/><TLN n="2343" /><QLN n="2337" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> In such a night

<L n="2268"/><TLN n="2347" /><QLN n="2341" /><S><SP norm="Jessica">Jessica</SP> In such a night

<L n="2271"/><TLN n="2350" /><QLN n="2344" />and nere a true one.</S>
<L n="2272"/><TLN n="2351" /><QLN n="2345" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> In such a night

<L n="2274"/><TLN n="2353" /><QLN n="2347" />slaunder her Loue, and he forgaue it her.</S>

<L n="2276"/><TLN n="2355" /><QLN n="2349" />But harke, I heare the footing of a man.</S>

<L n="2276.1"/><SD t="entrance">Enter a Messenger.</SD>
<L n="2277"/><TLN n="2357" /><QLN n="2351" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Who comes so fast in silence of the night?</S>
<L n="2278"/><TLN n="2358" /><QLN n="2352" /><S><SP norm="Messenger">Messenger</SP> A friend?</S>

<L n="2283"/><TLN n="2363" /><QLN n="2357" />by holy crosses where she kneeles and prayes
<L n="2284"/><TLN n="2364" /><QLN n="2358" />for happy wedlock houres.</S>
<L n="2285"/><TLN n="2365" /><QLN n="2359" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Who comes with her?</S>

<L n="2288"/><TLN n="2368" /><QLN n="2362" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> He is not, nor we haue not heard from him,

<L n="2291"/><TLN n="2371" /><QLN n="2365" />some welcome for the Mistres of the house.</S> 
<SD t="entrance"> Enter Clowne.</SD>
<L n="2292"/><TLN n="2372" /><QLN n="2366" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> Sola, sola: wo ha, ho sola, sola.</S>
<L n="2293"/><TLN n="2373" /><QLN n="2367" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Who calls?</S>
<L n="2294"/><TLN n="2374" /><QLN n="2368" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> Sola, did you see M. Lorenzo, & M. Lorenzo sola, sola.</S>
<L n="2295"/><TLN n="2375" /><QLN n="2369" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Leaue hollowing man, heere.</S>

<L n="2297"/><TLN n="2377" /><QLN n="2371" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Heere?</S>
<L n="2298"/><TLN n="2378" /><QLN n="2372" /><S><SP norm="Lancelot">Lancelot</SP> Tell him there's a Post come from my Maister, with his
<L n="2299"/><TLN n="2379" /><QLN n="2373" />horne full of good newes, my Maister will be heere ere morning
<L n="2300"/><TLN n="2380" /><QLN n="2374" />sweete soule.</S>

<L n="2301"/><TLN n="2381" /><QLN n="2375" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Let's in, and there expect their comming.
<L n="2302"/><TLN n="2382" /><QLN n="2376" />And yet no matter: why should we goe in.
<L n="2303"/><TLN n="2383" /><QLN n="2377" />My friend Stephen, signifie I pray you
<L n="2304"/><TLN n="2384" /><QLN n="2378" />within the house, your mistres is at hand,
<L n="2305"/><TLN n="2385" /><QLN n="2379" />and bring your musique foorth into the ayre.
<L n="2306"/><TLN n="2386" /><QLN n="2380" />How sweet the moone-light sleepes vpon this banke,
<L n="2307"/><TLN n="2387" /><QLN n="2381" />heere will we sit, and let the sounds of musique
<L n="2308"/><TLN n="2388" /><QLN n="2382" />creepe in our eares soft stilnes, and the night
<L n="2309"/><TLN n="2389" /><QLN n="2383" />become the tutches of sweet harmonie:
<L n="2310"/><TLN n="2390" /><QLN n="2384" />sit Iessica, looke how the floore of heauen
<L n="2311"/><TLN n="2391" /><QLN n="2385" />is thick inlayed with pattens of bright gold,
<L n="2312"/><TLN n="2392" /><QLN n="2386" />there's not the smallest orbe which thou beholdst
<L n="2313"/><TLN n="2393" /><QLN n="2387" />but in his motion like an Angell sings,
<L n="2314"/><TLN n="2394" /><QLN n="2388" />still quiring to the young eyde Cherubins;
<L n="2315"/><TLN n="2395" /><QLN n="2389" />such harmonie is in immortall soules,
<L n="2316"/><TLN n="2396" /><QLN n="2390" />but whilst this muddy vesture of decay
<L n="2317"/><TLN n="2397" /><QLN n="2391" />dooth grosly close it in, we cannot heare it:
<L n="2318"/><TLN n="2398" /><QLN n="2392" />Come hoe, and wake Diana with a himne,
<L n="2319"/><TLN n="2399" /><QLN n="2393" />with sweetest tutches pearce your mistres eare,
<L n="2320"/><TLN n="2400" /><QLN n="2394" />and draw her home with musique.</S> 
<SD t="sound"> play Musique.</SD>
<L n="2321"/><TLN n="2401" /><QLN n="2395" /><S><SP norm="Jessica">Jessica</SP> I am neuer merry when I heare sweet musique.</S>
<L n="2322"/><TLN n="2402" /><QLN n="2396" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> The reason is your spirits are attentiue:
<L n="2323"/><TLN n="2403" /><QLN n="2397" />for doe but note a wild and wanton heard
<L n="2324"/><TLN n="2404" /><QLN n="2398" />or race of youthfull and vnhandled colts
<L n="2325"/><TLN n="2405" /><QLN n="2399" />fetching mad bounds, bellowing and neghing loude,
<L n="2326"/><TLN n="2406" /><QLN n="2400" />which is the hote condition of their blood,
<L n="2327"/><TLN n="2407" /><QLN n="2401" />if they but heare perchance a trumpet sound,
<L n="2328"/><TLN n="2408" /><QLN n="2402" />or any ayre of musique touch their eares,
<L n="2329"/><TLN n="2409" /><QLN n="2403" />you shall perceaue them make a mutuall stand,
<L n="2330"/><TLN n="2410" /><QLN n="2404" />their sauage eyes turn'd to a modest gaze,
<L n="2331"/><TLN n="2411" /><QLN n="2405" />by the sweet power of musique: therefore the Poet
<L n="2332"/><TLN n="2412" /><QLN n="2406" />did faine that Orpheus drew trees, stones, and floods.
<L n="2333"/><TLN n="2413" /><QLN n="2407" />Since naught so stockish hard and full of rage,
<L n="2334"/><TLN n="2414" /><QLN n="2408" />but musique for the time doth change his nature,
<L n="2335"/><TLN n="2415" /><QLN n="2409" />the man that hath no musique in himselfe,
<L n="2336"/><TLN n="2416" /><QLN n="2410" />nor is not moued with concord of sweet sounds,
<L n="2337"/><TLN n="2417" /><QLN n="2411" />is fit for treasons, stratagems, and spoiles,

<L n="2338"/><TLN n="2418" /><QLN n="2412" />the motions of his spirit are dull as night,
<L n="2339"/><TLN n="2419" /><QLN n="2413" />and his affections darke as Terebus:
<L n="2340"/><TLN n="2420" /><QLN n="2414" />let no such man be trusted: marke the musique.</S>

<L n="2340.1"/><SD t="entrance">Enter Portia and Nerrissa.</SD>
<L n="2341"/><TLN n="2422" /><QLN n="2416" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> That light we see is burning in my hall:
<L n="2342"/><TLN n="2423" /><QLN n="2417" />how farre that little candell throwes his beames,
<L n="2343"/><TLN n="2424" /><QLN n="2418" />so shines a good deede in a naughty world.</S>
<L n="2344"/><TLN n="2425" /><QLN n="2419" /><S><SP norm="Nerissa">Nerissa</SP> When the moone shone we did not see the candle?</S>
<L n="2345"/><TLN n="2426" /><QLN n="2420" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> So dooth the greater glory dim the lesse,
<L n="2346"/><TLN n="2427" /><QLN n="2421" />a substitute shines brightly as a King
<L n="2347"/><TLN n="2428" /><QLN n="2422" />vntill a King be by, and then his state
<L n="2348"/><TLN n="2429" /><QLN n="2423" />empties it selfe, as doth an inland brooke
<L n="2349"/><TLN n="2430" /><QLN n="2424" />into the maine of waters: musique harke.</S>
<L n="2350"/><TLN n="2431" /><QLN n="2425" /><S><SP norm="Nerissa">Nerissa</SP> It is your musique Madame of the house?</S>
<L n="2351"/><TLN n="2432" /><QLN n="2426" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> Nothing is good I see without respect,
<L n="2352"/><TLN n="2433" /><QLN n="2427" />me thinks it sounds much sweeter then by day?</S>
<L n="2353"/><TLN n="2434" /><QLN n="2428" /><S><SP norm="Nerissa">Nerissa</SP> Silence bestowes that vertue on it Madam?</S>
<L n="2354"/><TLN n="2435" /><QLN n="2429" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> The Crow doth sing as sweetly as the Larke
<L n="2355"/><TLN n="2436" /><QLN n="2430" />when neither is attended: and I thinke
<L n="2356"/><TLN n="2437" /><QLN n="2431" />the Nightingale if she should sing by day
<L n="2357"/><TLN n="2438" /><QLN n="2432" />when euery Goose is cackling, would be thought
<L n="2358"/><TLN n="2439" /><QLN n="2433" />no better a Musition then the Renne?
<L n="2359"/><TLN n="2440" /><QLN n="2434" />How many things by season, seasond are
<L n="2360"/><TLN n="2441" /><QLN n="2435" />to their right prayse, and true perfection:
<L n="2361"/><TLN n="2442" /><QLN n="2436" />Peace, how the moone sleepes with Endimion,
<L n="2362"/><TLN n="2443" /><QLN n="2437" />and would not be awak'd.</S>
<L n="2363"/><TLN n="2444" /><QLN n="2438" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> That is the voyce,
<L n="2364"/><TLN n="2445" /><QLN n="2439" />or I am much deceau'd of Portia.</S>
<L n="2365"/><TLN n="2446" /><QLN n="2440" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> He knowes me as the blind man knowes the Cuckoe
<L n="2366"/><TLN n="2447" /><QLN n="2441" />by the bad voyce?</S>
<L n="2367"/><TLN n="2448" /><QLN n="2442" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Deere Lady welcome home?</S>
<L n="2368"/><TLN n="2449" /><QLN n="2443" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> We haue bin praying for our husbands welfare,
<L n="2369"/><TLN n="2450" /><QLN n="2444" />which speed we hope the better for our words:

<L n="2371"/><TLN n="2452" /><QLN n="2446" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Madam, they are not yet:
<L n="2372"/><TLN n="2453" /><QLN n="2447" />but there is come a Messenger before
<L n="2373"/><TLN n="2454" /><QLN n="2448" />to signifie their comming?</S>

<L n="2374"/><TLN n="2455" /><QLN n="2449" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> Goe in Nerrissa.
<L n="2375"/><TLN n="2456" /><QLN n="2450" />Giue order to my seruants, that they take
<L n="2376"/><TLN n="2457" /><QLN n="2451" />no note at all of our being absent hence,

<L n="2378"/><TLN n="2459" /><QLN n="2453" /><S><SP norm="Lorenzo">Lorenzo</SP> Your husband is at hand, I heare his trumpet,

<L n="2380"/><TLN n="2461" /><QLN n="2455" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> This night me thinks is but the day light sicke,

<L n="2382"/><TLN n="2463" /><QLN n="2457" />such as the day is when the sunne is hid.</S>

<L n="2407"/><TLN n="2490" /><QLN n="2484" /><S><SP norm="Nerissa">Nerissa</SP> What talke you of the posie or the valew:
<L n="2408"/><TLN n="2491" /><QLN n="2485" />You swore to me when I did giue you,

<L n="2409"/><TLN n="2492" /><QLN n="2486" />that you would weare it till your houre of death,
<L n="2410"/><TLN n="2493" /><QLN n="2487" />and that it should lie with you in your graue,

<L n="2415"/><TLN n="2498" /><QLN n="2492" /><S><SP norm="Gratiano">Gratiano</SP> He will, and if he liue to be a man.</S>
<L n="2416"/><TLN n="2499" /><QLN n="2493" /><S><SP norm="Nerissa">Nerissa</SP> I, if a woman liue to be a man.</S>
<L n="2417"/><TLN n="2500" /><QLN n="2494" /><S><SP norm="Gratiano">Gratiano</SP> Now by this hand I gaue it to a youth,

<L n="2422"/><TLN n="2505" /><QLN n="2499" /><S><SP norm="Portia">Portia</SP> You were to blame, I must be plaine with you,

<L n="2428"/><TLN n="2511" /><QLN n="2505" />I dare be sworne for him he would not leaue it,
